         <td><span class="Latinx" lang="ine-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h%E2%82%82%C3%A9b%C5%8Dl" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/h‚ÇÇ√©b≈?l">*h‚ÇÇ√©b≈?l</a></span></td>

      <p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href="/wiki/appel#Middle_English" title="appel">appel</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/%C3%A6ppel#Old_English" title="√¶ppel">√¶ppel</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">‚Äú</span><span class="mention-gloss">apple, fruit in general, ball</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">‚Ä?</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West       <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&action=edit&section=4" title="Edit section: Noun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 

      <p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">apple</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/apples#English" title="apples">apples</a></b>) </p> 

      <ol>

       <li>A <a href="/wiki/common" title="common">common</a>, <a href="/wiki/round" title="round">round</a> <a href="/wiki/fruit" title="fruit">fruit</a> produced by the <a href="/wiki/tree" title="tree">tree</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Malus_domestica" title="Malus domestica">Malus domestica</a></i>, cultivated in <a href="/wiki/temperate" title="temperate">temperate</a> climates. <span class="defdate">[from 9th c.]</span> <span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations ‚ñº</a></span>

        <ul style="display: none;">

         <li><b>c. 1378</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Langland" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:William Langland">William Langland</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piers_Plowman" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Piers Plowman">Piers Plowman</a></i>: 

          <dl>

           <dd>

            I prayed pieres to pulle adown an <b>apple</b>.

           </dd>

          </dl></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>1815</b> December (indicated as <b>1816</b>), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jane_Austen" class="extiw" title="w:Jane Austen">[Jane Austen]</a>, chapter IX, in <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emma_(novel)" class="extiw" title="w:Emma (novel)">Emma:<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="A Novel. In Three Volumes.">‚Ä¶</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite>, volume I, London: <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Printed [by]">‚Ä¶</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> [Charles Roworth and James Moyes] for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Murray_(publishing_house)" class="extiw" title="w:John Murray (publishing house)">John Murray</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://worldcat.org/oclc/1708336">1708336</a></small>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/emmanovelinthree131aust/page/n192/mode/1up">pages 184‚Äì185</a>:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">I have so often heard Mr. Woodhouse recommend a baked <b>apple</b>. I believe it is the only way that Mr. Woodhouse thinks the fruit thoroughly wholesome. We have <b>apple</b> dumplings, however, very often. Patty makes an excellent <b>apple</b>-dumpling.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>2013</b> October 28, John Vallins, ‚ÄúApples of Concord‚Ä?, in <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Guardian">The Guardian</a></cite>‚Äé<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2013/oct/28/somerset-apples-of-concord">[1]</a></sup>:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Close by and under cover, I watched the juicing process. <b>Apples</b> were washed, then tipped, stalks and all, into the crusher and reduced to pulp.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li>

        </ul></li> 

       <li>Any <a href="/wiki/fruit" title="fruit">fruit</a> or <a href="/wiki/vegetable" title="vegetable">vegetable</a>, or any other thing produced by a plant such as a <a href="/wiki/gall" title="gall">gall</a> or <a href="/wiki/cone" title="cone">cone</a>, especially if produced by a tree and similar to the fruit of <i><a href="/wiki/Malus_domestica" title="Malus domestica">Malus domestica</a></i>; also (with qualifying words) used to form the names of specific fruits such as <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/custard_apple#English" title="custard apple">custard apple</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/rose_apple#English" title="rose apple">rose apple</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/thorn_apple#English" title="thorn apple">thorn apple</a></i> etc. <span class="defdate">[from 9th c.]</span> <span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations ‚ñº</a></span>

            <i>Hippomane mancinella.</i> (Manchineel-tree.) Dr. Peysonnel relates that a soldier, who was a slave with the Turks, eat some of the <b>apples</b> of this tree, and was soon seized with a swelling and pain of the abdomen.

           </dd>

          </dl></li> 

         <li><b>1833</b>, Charles Williams, <i>The Vegetable World</i>, page 179: 

          <dl>

           <dd>

            One kind of <b>apple</b> or gall, inhabited only by one grub, is hard and woody on the outside, resembling a little wooden ball, of a yellowish color, but internally it is of a soft, spongy texture.

           </dd>

          </dl></li> 

         <li><b>1853</b>, Mrs. S. F. Cowper, <i>Country Rambles in England, Or, Journal of a Naturalist</i>, page 172: 

          <dl>

           <dd>

            The cross-bill will have seeds from the <b>apple</b>, or cone of the fir‚Äîthe green-finch, seeds from the uplands, or door of barn, or rick-yard.

           </dd>

          </dl></li> 

         <li><b>1889</b>, United States. Department of Agriculture, <i>Report of the Secretary of Agriculture</i>, page 376: 

          <dl>

           <dd>

            The "<b>apple</b>" or gall usually forms a somewhat kidney-shaped excrescence, attached by a small base on the concave side, and varying in size from a half an inch to an inch and a half in length.

           </dd>

          </dl></li>

        </ul></li>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=apple&action=edit&section=9" title="Edit section: Verb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 

      <p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">apple</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3|s|pres-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/apples#English" title="apples">apples</a></b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/appling#English" title="appling">appling</a></b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past|and|past|ptcp-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/appled#English" title="appled">appled</a></b>) </p> 

      <ol>

       <li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/transitive" title="transitive">transitive</a>, <a href="/wiki/intransitive" title="intransitive">intransitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To make or become apple-like. <span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations ‚ñº</a></span>

        <ul style="display: none;">

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>1992</b>, Marilyn Strathern, <cite>Reproducing the Future</cite>:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">One might say they have to be <b>appled</b>-up; varieties are selected for marketing which have the most apple-like qualities.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>2004</b>, Gregory David Roberts, <cite>Shantaram: A Novel</cite>:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">He glanced at me, his cheeks <b>appled</b> in the impish grin I was learning to recognise as the clever under-side of his broad and gentle smile.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>2007</b>, Claudia D. Newcorn, <cite>Crossover: Krisalys Chronicles of Feyree</cite>, page 35:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">A large smile <b>appled</b> his full cheeks as the four sprytes eagerly served themselves from the seeds and thinly sliced fruits.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>2011</b>, Cynthia Robinson, <cite>The Barbary Dogs</cite>, page 57:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">She smiled, and her cheeks <b>appled</b> up and her teeth were big and flat and her mouth was wide and spacious like an open invitation.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li>

        </ul></li> 

       <li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#obsolete" title="Appendix:Glossary">obsolete</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To form buds, bulbs, or fruit. <span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations ‚ñº</a></span>

        <ul style="display: none;">

         <li><b>1601</b> (1634), Philemon Holland (translator), <i>Pliny</i>, II, page 98: 

          <dl>

           <dd>

            Either they floure, or they <b>apple</b> or els be ready to bring forth fruit.

           </dd>

          </dl></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>1767</b>, James Justice, <cite>The British gardener's calendar</cite>, page 274:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">You may now sow upon moderate hot-beds, a few of the small Salad feeds, such as White Mustard, Rape, Cresses, and Cabbage Lettuces, and you may also sow upon other hot-beds, not to be drawn until they are pretty large and well <b>appled</b>, Radishes and Turnips, observing to sow them very thin, that the plants may have room to swell and grow;</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li> 

         <li><b>1796</b> (1800), Charles Marshall, <i>Gardening</i>, page 245: 

          <dl>

           <dd>

            The cabbage turnep is of two kinds; one <b>apples</b> above ground, and the other in it.

           </dd>

          </dl></li> 

         <li>

          <div class="citation-whole">

           <span class="cited-source"><b>1807</b>, <cite>The Complete Farmer</cite>:</span>

           <dl>

            <dd>

             <div class="h-quotation">

              <span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Other cultivators, however, advise "that the seed collected from a few turnips thus transplanted, should be preserved and sown in drills, in order to raise plants for see for the general crop, drawing out all such as are weak and improper, leaving only those that are strong and which take the lead; and that when these have <b>appled</b> or formed bulbs, to again take out such as do not appear good and perfect, as by this means turnip seed may be procured, not only of a more vigorous nature, but which is capable of vegetating with less moisture and which produces stronger and more hardy plants.</span>

             </div>

            </dd>

           </dl>

          </div></li>

        </ul></li>

      </ol>
